рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдЧрдиреНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдиреН рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрдпреЛрдЧрдВ рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдирдВ рдЪ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХреГрддреНрдп рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдХрд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░реАрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореАрдирд░рд╕рд┐рдВрд╣ рднрдЯреНрдЯрдорд╣реЛрджрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрднреВрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ, рдбрд╛. рд╡рд┐. рд╡рд░рджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдорд╣рд╛рд╢рдпрд╛рдГ рдЖрдЩреНрдЧреНрд▓рднрд╛рд╖рд╛рднреВрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд░реЗрдгрд╛рд╡рд░реНрдгрдпрдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ рди рддрддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рд╡рдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрдореН ред

рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдердХрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЙрддреНрддрдореВрд░реБрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ рдЕрдзрд┐рдЧрддрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдореАрдорд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдиреНрддрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐рддрдмрд╣реБрд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддрд╢рддрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрдд-рд╕рдореНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╡реЗрджрд╛рдиреНрддрджреЗрд╢рд┐рдХрдХреГрддрд╕рдХрд▓рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдГ рд╕рдХрд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрдХреБрд▓рд╕рдВрдорд╛рдирд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рдкрддрд┐рдкреБрд░- [[P2]] рд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдирд╡рджреЗрд╢рд┐рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд░реНрдердмрд┐рд░реБрджрд╛рдГ рд╡рд╛рджрдХреБрд╢рд▓рд╛рдГ рдирд╡рдирд╡реЛрдиреНрдореЗрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рднрд╛рд╕рдВрдкрдиреНрдирд╛рдГ рд╢рдорджрдорд╛рджреНрдпрдирдиреНрддрдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдЧреБрдгрдирд┐рдзрдпрдГ рд╕рджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╕рдВрдкрдиреНрдирд╛рдГ рднрд╛рд░рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╕реГрдорд░рдХреАрд░реНрддрдпреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдд ред рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд░реНрд╖реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рджрд┐рд╡рдВрдЧрддрд╛рд╢реН рдЪ ред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН рдПрд╡ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдХрддрд┐рдкрдпрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░-рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирдВ рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╡рд╢рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рдордореЗрддрд┐ рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕рдВрддреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред

рдЖрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдпреИрд╕реНрддреИрдГ рдХреГрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдп рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд▓рд┐рдкрд┐рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрдХрд░рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдгреЗрди рд╢реЛрдзрдирдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХрдВ рддрдВ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдареЗрд╜рддреНрд░ рдЖрдЧрдордХреЛрд╢рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдВ рдХреГрддрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рд╛рдореНрдкреНрд░рддрдореН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧреЗ рд╕рд╛рд╣рд┐рддреНрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрдкрджрдореН рдЕрдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдХреНрд╕реЗрдирд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛-рд░рд╛рдорд╛рдиреБрдЬрдЪрд░рд┐рддреНрд░рдЪрдореНрдкреВрдкреНрд░рднреГрддрд┐рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдиреН рдЖрдзреБрдирд┐рдХрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджреНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдарджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рддрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдЖрдЧрдо-рд╕рд╛рд╣рд┐рддреНрдпрдпреЛрдГ рд╡реИрджреБрд╖реНрдпрдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рд╢реНрд░реАрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореАрдирд░рд╕рд┐рдВрд╣рднрдЯреНрдЯ-рдорд╣реЛрджрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдХреГрддрдЬреНрдЮрддрд╛рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХрдВ рд╢реБрднрд╛рд╢рдВрд╕рдирдВ рдХрд░реЛрдорд┐, рдпреЗрди рдПрд╡рдВрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдирдкрд┐ рдмрд╣реБрддрд░рд╛рдиреН рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджреНрдп рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдард╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпреЗрдпреБрдГ ред

рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд╕реНрдп рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛, рдЖрдЩреНрдЧреНрд▓рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдЙрдкреЛрджреНрдШрд╛рддрд▓реЗрдЦрди рдПрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рддрд▓реНрд▓реЗрдЦрдирд╛рдп рдбрд╛. рд╡рд┐. рд╡рд░рджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдп рдорд╣реЛрджрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рддрд╛рдГ ред рддреЗ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд▓рдореНрдмрдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрдЪрд┐рд░рд╛рджреН рдПрд╡ рд╕рдореБрдЪрд┐рддрдореН рдЙрдкреЛрджреНрдШрд╛рддрдореН рдЖрдЩреНрдЧреНрд▓рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд▓рд┐рдЦреНрдп рджрддреНрддрд╡рдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдореБрд╣реБрд░реНрдореБрд╣реБрдГ рдХреГрддрдЬреНрдЮрддрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╡реЗрджрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред

рдРрд╣рд┐рдХрд╛рдореБрд╖реНрдорд┐рдХрд╕рдХрд▓рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде-рддрддреНрд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рд╡рдмреЛрдзрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд░рдореНрдпрдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирдкрд░реЛрд╜рдпрдВ рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдердГ рддрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердирд┐рд░реНрдзрд╛рд░рдгрдкрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдЖрд╕реНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдореЛрджрд╛рдп рдХрд▓реНрдкрддрд╛рдореН рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд╛рд╕реЗ ред

рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдардореН, рддрд┐рд░реБрдкрддрд┐рдГ ред
рдбрд╛. рдПрдиреН. рдПрд╕реН. рд░рд╛рдорд╛рдиреБрдЬрддрд╛рддрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдГ
рдХреБрд▓рдкрддрд┐рдГ

[[Pi]]

INTRODUCTION

The Veda-s are the oldest records of Indian tradition. The derivative sense of the word veda is that which provides a means to acquire knowledge of reality (tattva). Along with the veda-s, there has been, in existence, another stream of tradition called by the name agama. The Vedas are also called Nigama. The root gam which occurs in both these words means ’to know’, besides having the sense ’to go’. The agama-s are not anti-Vedic, as they are based on the Vedic tradition. They are therefore later than the Veda-s but definitely earlier to many later literary productions.

The Agama has some definite features which distinguish it from the Veda. At the same time, they reveal some marks akin to those of the Veda. Like the Veda, the agama is primarily concerned with the worship of God but of God in the form of an idol. Mandala (artistic and geometric drawings with coloured powders), Yantra (drawings in the form of circles in the metallic plate, the syllables of the mantra of a deity that is to be worshipped written in the petals of the lotus drawn in these circles), Mudr─Б (external gestures with the fingers assumed to certain positions to convey the items of worship) and others form part of the act of worship.

While the Veda-s have been admittedly an infallible authority for knowledge, the need for admitting the Agama as a course distinct from the Veda has to be justified. A very limited number of Brahmins, conversant with the ritualistic lore, performed the rituals in which they visualised the deity whom they invoked by the mantra-s. Others, who were twice-born, women and sudra-s could not have received such a vision. There is no surprise, if they too had a yearning to behold the deity. Besides, the women and sudra-s, who were disqualified for having upanayana (investiture with the sacred thread) and therefore could not study the Veda-s, had to remain content with the satisfaction that the ritual [[Pii]] is performed. The Agama came into being to provide these people with a concrete form for worship, which would endure to be available to them for all times.

Kashmir seems to have been the home of the Agama. The rivers Ganga and Yamuna are stated in the Pa├▒car─Бtra Agama to flow in the east, and south-east respectively thereby indicating that the region where this text should have been available then must be respectively in the west and north-west of the regions through which Ganga and Yamuna flowed. Saraswati flowed to the south of that region which should be Kashmir.1 God’s grace is called ┼Ъaktip─Бta, alighting of power. This word occurs only in the Agama texts written in Kashmir.2 The Yantra is to be prepared in the birch bark by drawing the diagrams. This bark is available only in Kashmir.3

Regarding the name Pa├▒car─Бtra, there is a lot of confused accounts for determining its sense. Most of them are ingenous and are incorrect also. The word Pa├▒car─Бtra is a compound made up of two parts pa├▒ca and r─Бtra. The former denotes the number and the latter means the day and night together (ahor─Бtra). Any explanation for this word should convey the significance of these two parts Whatever be the explanation offered in the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts, the reasonable explanation lies in taking the name to refer to the five divisions of the day made in this Agama for purposes of attending to the worship of God at the particular parts of the day marked by these divisions.4

Another interpretation deserves consideration. N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa is stated to have taught five sages the doctrines of the system. The names of these sages are given as ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нilya, Aupag─Бyana, Mau├▒jy─Бyana, Kau┼Ыika and Bharadv─Бja.5 Here, r─Бtra must be taken to mean not in the sense of the whole day (ahor─Бtra) but day with a part of the night included. Since these sages were promulgators of the doctrines of the system, the name Pa├▒car─Бtra could have been given to this system. Yet, it is hardly possible to believe that the name of a system could have been given on the number of promulgators or teachers who preached those doctrines. There is also the difficulty of explaining the word r─Бtra in this interpretation.

The ─Аgamas are of two kinds, as far as Vaiс╣гс╣Зavism is concerned. They are Vaikh─Бnasa and Pa├▒car─Бtra. The former is based on the purely Vedic traditions. The latter, has a Tantric character.

Many arguments are advanced questioning the authority of the Pa├▒car─Бtra. Firstly, T─Бntrika mantra-s are used in the place of the Vedic mantras. ┼Ъ┼лdras and women are allowed to undergo initiation for worshipping God which runs against the authority of the Vedic and Ved─Бс╣Еga authority.6 The Vedic rituals enjoining invocation (─Бv─Бhana) and send-off (visarjana) to the deities during ritualistic performances are given up. Contrary to this, the deity is worshipped in the concrete form of the idol.

Secondly, the Brahmas┼лtra-s condemn the authority of the Pa├▒car─Бtra on the ground that the soul with the name Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa is stated here as born of V─Бsudeva. Similarly, Pradyumna and Aniruddha who are mind and ego are born respectively of Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa and Pradyumna. Neither the self is born nor mind and ego spring out of the self or mind. Therefore the Pa├▒car─Бtra, which thus flouts the authority of the Vedas, cannot be admitted as authentic.

Thirdly, ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нilya is stated in the Paramasaс╣Бhit─Б,7 a Pa├▒car─Бtra text, to have become disappointed by not getting what is good from the study of the Vedas and Ved─Бс╣Еgas. He acquired what was good for him by a study of the Pa├▒car─Бtra. This goes against Vedic authority and questions the validity of the Vedas. This proves the invalidity of the Pa├▒car─Бtra.

Lastly, the Vaikh─Бnasa texts contain severe criticism of the validity of this ─Аgamas.8 On these grounds, the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama is held to lack in authority and so is to be discarded.

[[Piv]]
While answering these objections, it is necessary to take note of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama’s attitude to the Veda. Vedic mantras are profusely cited in the ─Аgama texts.9 These are in addition to the T─Бntrika mantra-s that are enjoined for each practice. The name Saс╣Бhit─Б to the ─Аgama texts such as S─Бttvatasaс╣Бhit─Б, Pauс╣гkarasaс╣Бhit─Б and others, use of various kinds of fire pits (Kuс╣Зс╕Нa)10 for performing homa, names y─Бga and ijy─Б for worship, and the word avabhс╣Ыtha referring to the concluding session of the mahotsava, all go to show that the ┼Ъrauta practices had a deep influence on the ─Аgama-s. This resulted in the use of the above mentioned expressions for attending to the worship of God.

The entire population comprises of women and ┼Ъ┼лdras with few exceptions. These people were denied Upanayana and consequently could not perform worship. It is the liberal outlook of the ─Аgama to boldly prescribe T─Бntrika mantra-s for these people. The idol is thus brought in to be worshipped by them. This practice is not anti-Vedic but non-Vedic.

Validity of the Pa├▒car─Бtra system which is assailed in the Brahmas┼лtra-s, is defended by Y─Бmun─Бc─Бrya in his ─Аgamapr─Бm─Бс╣Зya and by R─Бm─Бnuja following him in his ┼Ъr─лbh─Бс╣гya, Ved─Бntas─Бra and Ved─Бntad─лpa. The Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita school, holds that Vy─Бsa, who maintained the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama as valid in the ┼Ъ─Бntiparvan of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata, would not have rejected its validity in the Brahmas┼лtra-s composed by him. Hence, it is prudent to take the s┼лtra-s (2.2.39 & 40) as conveying the points for rejection of validity to Pa├▒car─Бtra and the other two s┼лtra-s (2.2.41&42) as defending its validity and establishing it. Besides, the Pa├▒car─Бtra system nowhere declares the soul as having birth.

Thirdly, ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нilya’s saying that he could get the good which we wanted from the Pa├▒car─Бtra and not the Veda does not mean that he decried the authority of the Veda. It means only that he could not get the good from the Veda and so expresses his inability to get it.

[[Pv]]
Lastly, the Vaikh─Бnasa’s attack on the Pa├▒car─Бtra is due to rivalry between the Vaikh─Бnas─Б and Pa├▒car─Бtra followers who sought to acquire more power and emoluments in cash and kind from the temples. This bitter attack on the Pa├▒car─Бtra is contained in all the available works of the Vaikh─Бnas─Б system. The Ratnatraya, Lakс╣гm─л tantra, Ahirbudhnya Saс╣Бhit─Б, Sanatkum─Бra Saс╣Бhit─Б and other early texts do not contain even a single reference against the Vaikh─Бnasa system or its inferiority. Ved─Бnta De┼Ыika brushes aside this mutual attack and points to its rise as the work of mischief mongers who exploit such situations.11

Validity of the Pa├▒car─Бtra is indicated in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata,12 ─Аgamaс╕Нambara13 and Spandaprad─лpik─Б.14 Thus validity of Pa├▒car─Бtra stands unassailed.

The long period of development of the Pa├▒car─Бtra system could be roughly divided into two stages. The date or period marking one stage from another could not be fixed. The first stage had both the theoretical and practical aspects of the system developed to a remarkable degree. Ultimate Reality is stated to be Brahman identified with Viс╣гс╣Зu.15 ┼Ъakti, the female principle, is ever associated with Him and the two are held to be one reality. Unlike the S─Бс╣Еkhya system, and like the ┼Ъ─Бkta and ┼Ъaiva ─Аgama-s, the Pa├▒car─Бtra treats ┼Ъakti as sentient and active. It accounts for the creation, maintenance and dissolution of the universe. It is called by the name Lakс╣гm─л. The supreme form of both is one of knowledge. Viс╣гс╣Зu, who is also stated to have the names N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa, Bhagav─Бn and V─Бsudeva, possesses six qualities J├▒─Бna-Knowledge, ai┼Ыvarya-lordship, bala-strength, v─лrya-virility, ┼Ыakti-potency and tejas-splendour. These constitute into a group called с╣в─Бс╕Нguс╣Зya. Viс╣гс╣Зu and ┼Ъr─л are held to have this group as their body.16

Creation is held to be of three kinds, pure, mixed (of pure and impure). The first marks the stage when ┼Ъakti emanates to give relief to the souls which are in bondage. Ultimate Reality divides itself into V─Бsudeva, Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa, Pradyumna and Aniru- [[Pvi]] ddha, the succeeding form arising from the preceding one. Each one has all the six qualities, yet the purpose of this division is to enable the universe to be dissolved through Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa who possesses j├▒─Бna and bala to a relatively high degree. He is also in charge of spreading the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama. Pradyumna has a preponderance of v─лrya and ai┼Ыvarya and attends to the work of maintaining the created world in a stable condition. He attends to the practise of the ─Аgama principles. Creation is attended to by Aniruddha with excess of ┼Ыakti and tejas. He rewards the results of the deeds done by people.

The mixed kind of creation is marked by the emanations of Brahm─Б, Viс╣гс╣Зu and Rudra and their consorts. The impure kind is of material nature following the principles of the S─Бс╣Бkhya system.

Viс╣гс╣Зu is stated to take five forms called Para, Vy┼лha, Vibhava, Arc─Б and Antary─Бmin. Para is the transcendental form. Vibhava includes the ten divine descents (avat─Бra) and also thirty eight,17 or thirty nine forms,18 which He takes from time to time. Arc─Б represents God in the form of idol, which He though formless, takes this finite form to show favour to His devotees.19 The form of Antary─Бmin is to remain within the self and control it by directing it to lead a virtuous way of life, of course in accordance with the residues of the deeds done by it.

Regarding the means of getting freedom from bondage, Karma, J├▒─Бna, Yoga and Prapatti are enjoined.20 These are to be practised in the light of the five-fold classification of the daily routine. In particular, Prapatti gets a very detailed treatment in the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama,21 Release from bondage is of the nature of close communion (S─Бyujya) with God.

Treatment of mantra-s, their varieties and their component parts receive an elaborate treatment in the Lakс╣гm─лtantra, Ahirbudhnya Saс╣Бhit─Б and Jay─Бkhya Saс╣Бhit─Б. Influence of the Vedic practises is felt in this ─Аgama where God is treated as Mantradeha, [[Pvii]] having mantra for His body. The mantras are to be used with accuracy of pronunciation and accent. Any one cannot undertake the act of worship. Initiation (d─лkс╣г─Б) is a preliminary must for every individual. The process is very elaborate, with much responsibility thrown on the priest who initiates his pupils. Worship of the idol is enjoined and this is called B─Бhiry─Бga, external worship. Mentally, the worshipper must undertake the act of worship (antary─Бga) and this should precede B─Бhiry─Бga. Yantra, Maс╣Зс╕Нala, Ny─Бsa and Mudr─Б play a leading role in the acts of worship. All these are treated in great detail in the Ratnatraya (S─Бttvata, Pauс╣гkara and J─Бy─Бkhyasaс╣Бhit─Б-s), Lakс╣гm─л tantra and Ahirbudhnyasaс╣Бhit─Б. There is however no reference in these texts to the details about building of temples, installation of the idol, conduct of the festivals and others. It is safe to hold that the first stage in the development of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama could have come to an end with the rise of these texts. Perhaps, the period may be fixed tentatively about 800 A.D.

The second stage is marked by ceaseless activity on the part of the rich patrons (Yajam─Бna) to promote building temples and arranging for the installation of the idols and for the celebration of the festivals. Most of the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts, other than the five mentioned above, treat these matters. It is at this period, the matters dealt with in the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts, as doctrines in theory and practise, were classified under four heads, J├▒─Бnap─Бda, Yogap─Бda, Kriy─Бp─Бda and Cary─Бp─Бda. The first section deals with the nature of reality like Brahman, ┼Ъakti, creation and others. The second enjoins the practise of Yoga as a means of visualising God within one’s own self. Kriy─Б refers to the building of temples and installation of idols there. Cary─Б treats the conduct of daily and occasional festivals, acts of expiation for lapses and work of renovation when there is disrepair in temples. Worship done to the idos in temples is called Par─Бrtha Yajana (worship for others’ sake) and to the idol or ┼Ъ─Бligr─Бma in houses called Sv─Бrthayajana (worship for one’s own sake).

[[Pviii]]
It is surprising to note that Pa├▒casaс╣Бsk─Бra22 does not get the treatment in the earlier texts of this ─Аgama. This is treated in the Parame┼Ыvara, Viс╣гс╣Зu tattva, P─Бr─Б┼Ыarya saс╣Бhit─Б, Parameс╣гс╣нhya saс╣Бhit─Б, Bh─Бradv─Бja saс╣Бhit─Б, Sanat-Kum─Бra saс╣Бhit─Б, N─Бrad─лya saс╣Бhit─Б and ─к┼Ыvara saс╣Бhit─Б, which are later than the earlier texts.23 The practise is of very ancient origin as evidenced from the voluminous citations found in Ved─Бnta De┼Ыika’s Saccaritarakс╣г─Б. The later texts of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama make this as obligatory.

The texts of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama in print and manuscripts are stated to be 108 in number.24 There are however 225 works, some of which are fragmentary enumerated in the introduction to the Lakс╣гm─лtantra.25 The texts are mostly ancient and could hardly be assigned to any particular period and in a chronological order. Yet, the Ratnatraya26 are held to be the earliest. The S─Бttvatasaс╣Бhit─Б devotes itself mainly to the worship of Vy┼лha and Vibhava deities. Initiation is also dealt with at length. Maс╣Зс╕Нala-s and shrines get an elaborate treatment in the Pauс╣гkarasaс╣Бhit─Б. The Jay─Бkhyasaс╣Бhit─Б contains an elaborate treatment of the Mantra-s, creation, worship, initiation and Ny─Бsa. The Lakс╣гm─л tantra, has the ┼Ъ─Бkta element. It is devoted mainly to the role played by ┼Ъakti in the system. Creation, Mantra-s, Ny─Бsa, worship and Prapatti receive a detailed treatment. Mantra-s and yantra-s are treated in detail in the Ahirbudhnya Saс╣Бhit─Б. Supreme importance is assigned in this work to Sudar┼Ыana. The ─к┼Ыvarasaс╣Бhit─Б is based on the S─Бttvata and is adopted in the temple at Melkote. Based on the Pauс╣гkarasaс╣Бhit─Б is the Parame┼Ыvarasaс╣Бhit─Б. This is practised in the temple at ┼Ъr─лraс╣Еgam. It is highly informative. The P─Бdmasaс╣Бhit─Б, which is adopted in the temple at K─Б├▒c─л, is based on the Jay─Бkhyasaс╣Бhit─Б. It is a very long text divided into four p─Бda-s and contains almost all the aspects of the ─Аgama fully treated. It is the only text containing all the p─Бdas. It is very much in use in most of the Pa├▒car─Бtra governed temples. The Paramasaс╣Бhit─Б is also an ancient text and treats many topics such as creation, initiation and installation. The Sanatkum─Бra Saс╣Бhit─Б is divided into five sections called Brahmar─Бtra, ┼Ъivar─Бtra, Indrar─Бtra, с╣Ъс╣гir─Бtra and Bс╣Ыhaspatir─Бtra, the last of which is lost.

[[Pix]]
Sage Sanatkum─Бra received information on several topics from Brahm─Б, ┼Ъiva, Indra, sages and Bс╣Ыhaspati. Hence his name is given in the title of the text. This text refers to Viс╣гс╣Зuliс╣Еga27 and Viс╣гс╣Зu as having forms in gradations; Viс╣гс╣Зu, Mah─Бviс╣гс╣Зu and Sad─Бviс╣гс╣Зu.28 Among others, the following could be mentioned for the treatment of the system, each containing some speciality for the nature of the topics. N─Бrad─лyasaс╣Бhit─Б, P─Бr─Б┼Ыarasaс╣Бhit─Б, Bh─Бradv─Бjasaс╣Бhit─Б, M─Бrkaс╣Зс╕Нeyasaс╣Бhit─Б, Vi┼Ыv─Бmitrasaс╣Бhit─Б, Viс╣гс╣Зutattva, Viс╣гс╣Зutilaka, Viс╣гс╣Зusaс╣Бhit─Б and ┼Ъr─лpra┼Ыnasaс╣Бhit─Б.

This ─Аgama received detailed treatment at the hands of Y─Бmun─Бc─Бrya (10th century) and Ved─Бntade┼Ыika (1268-1369). Validity of the Pa├▒car─Бtra is firmly established by Y─Бmun─Бc─Бrya in his ─Аgama Pr─Бm─Бс╣Зya. The Pa├▒car─Бtс╣Ыarakс╣г─Б of the Ved─Бntade┼Ыika is a valuable text as it deals with the Siddh─Бnta-s which are four in number, Pa├▒cak─Бla prakriy─Б and a commentary on R─Бm─Бnuj─Б’s Nitya. These works of the two ─Аc─Бrya-s do not refer to temple construction and conduct of festivals. Many manuals were in later days written on the system. Among them, specific mention must be made of the Kriy─Бkairavacandrik─Б of Var─Бhaguru. It deals with the Kriy─Б and Cary─Б aspects of the system. Tantras─Бra of Ved─Бntar─Бm─Бnuja of the last century is an important work on the Siddh─Бntas and practises of the Pa├▒car─Бtra system.

The latest addition to the Pa├▒car─Бtra is the Pa├▒car─Бtс╣Ыap─Бramya, now published for which the introduction is contained here. This work is the mature production of the erudite Vidw─Бn T. V─лrar─Бghav─Бch─Бrya. He was fully conversant with the fundamental doctrines of all the systems of Indian Philosophy. With his amazingly analytical intellect he did make use of his learning for interpreting the most obstruse problems in Indian philosophy which baffled many scholars.

The Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama holds ultimate reality to be Lakс╣гm─лn─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa, thus revealing the vaiс╣гс╣Зava character. The Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita Ved─Бnta is Vaiс╣гс╣Зavite to the core. For a long time, the two had been kept apart from each other. Adoption of the Pa├▒cak─Бlaprakriy─Б to govern the routine life of a Paramaik─Бntin,29 Pa├▒casaс╣Бsk─Бra, Pra- [[Px]] patti and the process of attending to daily worship to God, generally in the houses mark the practises, which have been in vogue in the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava families. These bear the full influence of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama. No attempt seems to have been made till recently to effect the rapproachment between the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama and the Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita Ved─Бnta. The place given to temple worship, conduct of festivals and temple building are governed, as far as Vaiс╣гс╣Зavism is concerned by the Pa├▒car─Бtra and Vaikh─Бnasa rules and regulations. The attraction which the people are provided with these has resulted in treating these as the only items and topics dealt with in the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava ─Аgama-s. The theological, cosmological and philosophical aspects of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama have been completely forgotten. It is these aspects that form the foundations for the edifice of Kriy─Б and Cary─Б p─Бda-s of the ─Аgama. These are dealt with in the Upaniс╣гads, Ved─Бnta texts and Dharma┼Ы─Бstra-s. The epics and Pur─Бс╣Зa-s contain sufficient information on the principles and practises of Vaiс╣гс╣Зavism. There cannot exist two sources for Vaiс╣гс╣Зavism in the forms of ─Аgama and Veda-s and sources based on the Veda-s. It is the duty of the learned to examine these two sources and determine the nature of Vaiс╣гс╣Зavism on a comparative and harmonious study of these two sources. The author of this book has successfully carried out this duty. His attempt is found in the main, to find that the two sources are not at variance with each other and supports this conclusion by drawing evidences from the ─Аgama-s and the sources based on the Veda-s. The evidences so collected are subjected with great care and skill, to a critical inquiry doing adequate justice to their prestige in the sources without loss of vigour and precision.

There are nearly sixty headings under which the Pa├▒car─Бtra is shown to be supreme. The topics dealt with in them are sometimes terse for comprehension and are also presented with well-reasoned arguments. To attempt at bringing out even the substance of each is an uphill task. Adequate justice cannot also be done to a brief treatment of the important topics. Therefore an attempt could be made only to offer a brief reference to some of them.

[[Pxi]]
At the outset, it is shown that gods possess forms, a matter which is seriously challenged by the M─лm─Бс╣Бsak─Бs particularly by Kum─Бrila Bhaс╣нс╣нa. This is briefly set aside by showing that Vy─Бsa, the author of the Brahmas┼лtras was in favour of admitting Gods’ possession of forms.

┼Ъaс╣Еkara is held to have declared the Pa├▒car─Бtra system as invalid on the ground that it mentions the soul. Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa to have been born out of V─Бsudeva, ┼Ъaс╣Еkara does not reject the Vy┼лha concept or the Pa├▒cak─Бlaprakriy─Б. Yet, he takes objection to the treatment of the Vy┼лha deities as not different from V─Бsudeva. This objection cannot stand, since the divine descents of Viс╣гс╣Зu (V─Бsudeva) as R─Бma and Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa will have to be treated as losing divinity and not descents at all. ┼Ъaс╣Еkara admits in a different context,30 the vy┼лha concept. Hence the objection is flimsy. The Bh─Бmat─л, Kalpataru and Parimala, which are commentary, subcommentary and commentary on the subcommentary on ┼Ъaс╣Еkara’s Brahmas┼лtrabh─Бс╣гya - argue that Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama contains the expressions of God N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and so could not be held as invalid. The passage on which the objection is based occurs in the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama. This passage will have to be explained without contradiction to the statements of the Vedas which declare that the soul is eternal. Reconciliation between the two statements should be made by taking the word birth in its secondary sense. Through Kс╣Ыtv─Б cint─Б, what is contradictory is first admitted and then rejected. Thus the statement of the birth of the soul is only apparently opposed to the Vedas and therefore the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama is valid.

To the question as to how the qualities j├▒─Бna and others be themselves the possessor of them, the answer is that identity of this kind is found in the Vedic pasages like ‘Food is verily the vital air’ (annaс╣Б vai pr─Бс╣Зaс╕е).31

[[Pxii]]
That Saс╣Бkarс╣гaс╣Зa and other two deities of the Vy┼лha are also V─Бsudeva is elaborately discussed by citing passages from the Lakс╣гm─лtantra and Ahirbudhnyasaс╣Бhit─Б. That ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нilya had to study the Pa├▒car─Бtra to get what he could not from the Vedic and allied texts is fully analysed by bringing a large number of passages from the Viс╣гс╣Зutilaka, ─Аgama pr─Бm─Бс╣Зya and ┼Ъr─лbh─Бс╣гya and is settled as authentic. In this context, the Piс╣гс╣нapa┼Ыuy─Бga, which is described in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata as performed by Uparicara Vasu, is upheld as authoritative, with carefully arranged citations from various sources.

The P─Б┼Ыupata system is rejected in the Brahmas┼лtras 2.2.37-41 on the ground that it maintains that Pa┼Ыupati (┼Ъiva) is the instrumental cause of the world. This goes against the Upaniс╣гadic doctrine that Brahman is both the material and instrumental cause, and therefore it is refuted like S─Бс╣Бkhya, Yoga, Ny─Бya and other systems.

┼Ъr─лkaс╣Зс╣нa, the author of a commentary on the Brahmas┼лtras, contends that the P─Б┼Ыupata system is two fold, authoritative and unauthoritative. The latter includes the V─Бm─Бc─Бra practises and therefore is impure. It includes within its fold the L─Бguс╕Нa, K─Бp─Бlika, K─Бl─Бmukha and others which are nonvedic and is therefore condemned in the Brahmas┼лtras. These are thus ┼Ъaс╣Бkara too refuted. The former kind is Vedic. To maintain that Brahman, as ┼Ъiva, is both the material and instrumental cause in this system, ┼Ъr─лkaс╣Зс╣нa takes such passages from the ┼Ъaiv─Бgama texts which are shown to convey that ┼Ъiva is the material cause and seeks to support the authority of the P─Б┼Ыupata system. Other passages in the ┼Ъaiva ─Аgama are shown to be either invalid or as admitting some other purport. The author rejects this interpretation, since s┼лtra 2.2.37 declares that there is inadequacy (as─Бma├▒jasya) in the argument of having ┼Ъiva as the Supreme deity. There is no adequate reason in support of this contention. Veda cannot justify this, as the P─Б┼Ыupata system admits Veda as the composition of God. Pa┼Ыupati is to be proved at first as the Supreme Being. This cannot be achieved through the Veda. The ┼Ъaiv─Бgama cannot be of any help, as it is held to have been promulgated for deceiving others. ┼Ъiva is held to be the instrumental cause. He is not omniscient and so [[Pxiii]] there is no adequate evidence in admitting the authority of the P─Б┼Ыupata system. On the contrary, there is nothing wanting in the Pa├▒car─Бtra system to be admitted as Vedic except the theory of the soul’s birth.

After showing that objections could not be raised against validity of the Pa├▒car─Бtra, the author establishes harmonious blending of the Pa├▒car─Бtra and the Bhagavadg─лt─Б. Advocating the means of devotion, the Lord asks Arjuna to take to Karmayoga with reference to God.32 R─Бm─Бnuja gives a theistic interpretation to Karmayoga by taking Karma to stand for building of temples, gardens, lighting the lamps, sweeping the yards, bringing flowers, offering worship, singing the praise of God and others.33 Worship of God is stated at the outset in the G─лt─Б while dealing with Karmayoga.34 Use of the petals of flowers, fruits and others could be offered only to the form of idol of God. It must be noted here that the Var─Бhapur─Бс╣Зa enjoins the use of the T─Бntrika mantras, if the Vedic mantras are not available.35 This enriches the worth of the Pa├▒car─Бtr─Бgama which enjoins the use of T─Бntrika Mantras.

With great ingenuity, the author remarks that N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa himself gave out Pa├▒car─Бtra, meaning that He who is the purport of the Veda is himself is the author of the Pa├▒car─Бtra. Karmayoga is only worship of God in the form of idol. R─Бma, a descendant of the sun (Vivasv─Бn), worshipped ┼Ъr─л Raс╣Еgan─Бtha. Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa tells in the G─лt─Б that He taught this Karmayoga to sun (Vivasv─Бn), who taught it to Manu. Manu gave it to Ikс╣гv─Бku of the solar dynasty.36 Worship of God in the form of the idol is thus emphasised in the G─лt─Б.

The Pa├▒car─Бtr─Бgama is closely allied to the Veda. The duties enjoined in the ┼Ъrautas┼лtras are to be followed. Vai┼Ыvadeva, a rite enjoined by the smс╣Ыtis is to be done after offering the food preparations to God.37 The Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama is mainly devoted to the worship of God. Therefore, it cannot be expected to contain information as to how life is to be lead on occasions other than attending to the worship of God. Secular activities also will have to be attended to, for which the guidelines are contained in the Dharma and Gс╣Ыhya s┼лtras and in the Dharma┼Ы─Бstras. There is the need for a P─Б├▒car─Бtrika to follow the texts based on the three vedas.38

[[Pxiv]]
Now a question arises as to what explanation is to be given to the passage. “One who undertakes yoga and enters into a meditative mood will feel that he is Brahman”. He is still like a pillar and does not enjoy the objects of life. This passage suggests that here there is the experience that Brahman and the soul are one. This would mean that this passage supports the sense of the Upaniс╣гadic passage ‘I am Brahman’… Besides, according to Bh┼лta┼Ыuddhi39 described in the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama, the aspirant loses the imperfect material body and assumes a non-material body. It is said that here the aspirant becomes God and worships Him.

In answer to this, the author states that the soul is identical with Brahman only by being the body of Brahman and that could not exist without Brahman. In the other case, the aspirant must be taken to mean that he had then got a form purified for acquiring fitness for performing worship. Or, the soul becomes God, that is, gets Brahman as the inner controller of his body.

The Pa├▒car─Бtra system is held to be based on Ek─Бyana veda. This veda is stated to be the root of the Vedas. King Bhoja is said to have referred to it. It is further said that this nature of the Ek─Бyana┼Ы─Бkh─Б was dealt with in the K─Б┼Ыm─лr─Бgamapr─Бm─Бс╣Зya.40 Pa├▒car─Бtra, is based on the statement-“There is no other way to get out of this world”41, and so no argument will be effective to set aside full validity to the P─Б├▒car─Бtr─Бgama.

A system must give information on tattva Reality. The Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama is shown by the author to deal with the nature of ultimate Reality. Passages are profusely cited from the Pauс╣гkara and Padma saс╣Бhit─Бs. Brahman is formless.42 Treatment of с╣в─Бс╕Нguс╣Зya in the Ahirbudhnyasaс╣Бhit─Б43 is stated by the author as very helpful in declaring Brahman as Saguс╣Зa. It is shown that many passages from the Upaniс╣гads are not properly explained in the systems of ┼Ъaс╣Бkara and Bh─Бskara. Such passages become meaningful only when the expressions occuring in the source books are interpreted by taking Brahman as saguс╣Зa.

[[Pxv]]
The Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama treats the soul to be of the size of the triad (trasareс╣Зu), but the Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita system does not admit this and maintains the size to be of that of the atom. R─Бm─Бnuja’s system does not also admit oneness (aikya) of Brahman with the soul which is however admitted in the Pa├▒car─Бtra system. The author expresses his disagreement with this Pa├▒car─Бtra doctrine. Three kinds of the released state are stated in the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts.44 They are of the nature of difference, non-difference and an admixture of both. The released state becomes marked by service. The released souls do then service to God. The second kind is one of intense identity between the Brahman and the soul. The soul then realises that it is Brahman. In the third kind, the Lord is made by the soul get delighted by worship. This is from the attitude of difference. Oneness is achieved from the angle of non-difference. The author observes that which among difference and non-difference marks the state of release could not be settled in this case. In a different context, attainment of bliss is stated in the Pa├▒car─Бtra text, to mark the state of release.45 The author shows that this must be admitted as the doctrine of the Pa├▒car─Бtra and so the soul is different from Brahman in the state of release.

The Pa├▒car─Бtra texts accord to ┼Ъr─л a place of position equal to that of Viс╣гс╣Зu. The author cites passages from the Lakс╣гm─л tantra to explain the position of ┼Ъr─л. The Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita system follows closely the ─Аgama in admitting ┼Ъr─л’s place. Like Viс╣гс╣Зu, ┼Ъr─л also is the means and goal.

Pa├▒car─Бtra is also called Siddh─Бnta and is of four kinds with the names ─Аgamasiddh─Бnta, Mantrasiddh─Бnta, Tantrasiddh─Бnta and Tantr─Бntarasiddh─Бnta. The author argues that ─Аgamasiddh─Бnta was practised in the Kс╣Ыtayuga and is now lost. The three texts S─Бttvata, Pauс╣гkara and J─Бy─Бkhyasaс╣Бhit─Бs belong to the Mantrasiddh─Бnta. The practises that are recommended for worshipping the departed souls are not exclusively attached or drawn from one of the Ratnatraya. The author offers a well reasoned treatment for the classification of the ─Аgamas according to the Siddh─Бntas [[Pxvi]] the three guс╣Зas sattva, rajas and tamas. His discussion is helpful to understand Ved─Бntade┼Ыika’s treatment of this matter in the Pa├▒car─Бtс╣Ыarakс╣г─Б.

How the mantras are to be formed afresh and analysed are treated only in the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts. Gross, subtle and transcendental aspects of important mantras are treated in the Ahirbudhnyasaс╣Бhit─Б.46 The Vaikh─Бnasas too have to depend upon the Pa├▒car─Бtra rules for the method of doing japa of important mantras. Every act of daily routine could be done in accordance with the dictates of one’s own s┼лtra. Yet, the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts declare that the Pa├▒car─Бtra mode of worship is supreme. Prapatti is admitted as a means of mokс╣гa in the Vaikh─Бnasa system. However, its treatment is available only in the Pa├▒car─Бtra texts. The Vaikh─Бnasas too have to turn to the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama, for information on some of the religious issues.

To The tradition of the Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas is found to depend very much on the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Бgama to get information on important issues and get problems resolved only through the contents of this ─Бgama. The community of the Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas, is much indebted to the authority of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Бgama.

Much dialectical skill is revealed by the author of this work in solving the problems of interpretation of crucial passages in the Upaniс╣гads, Dharma┼Ы─Бstras and Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Бgama. Quite often, he draws references to the Vaikh─Бnasa ─Аgama and offers a comparative note on the treatment of the topics in the Pa├▒car─Бtra and Vaikh─Бnasa ─Бgamas. He has successfully undertaken a study of the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Бgama in the light of ┼Ъr─лvaiс╣гс╣Зavasamprad─Бya and has done due justice to both without any partisanic attitude.

┼Ъr─л Vidw─Бn Uttam┼лr V─лrar─Бghav─Бch─Бrya who had done yeoman service to Sanskrit ┼Ъ─Бstras by editing many rare and standard works with his splendid commentaries, is the author of this work Pa├▒car─Бtra p─Бramya. It will be a futile exercise to expatiate on the nature of the contribution he has made to the Pa├▒car─Бtra ─Аgama through this work.

[[Pxvii]]
Rashtriya Sanskrit Vidyapeetha, Tirupati has undertaken the publication of this work. This is just the beginning of the interest which it displays in the pursuit of promotion of Sanskrit Studies, particularly ┼Ъ─Бstras which are the foundations of Hindu culture. It is hoped that more and more works of this kind would be published in the years to come, much to the delight and appreciation of Sanskrit scholars in India and abroad.

Paс╣Зс╕Нit Lakс╣гm─лnarasiс╣Бha Bhaс╣нс╣нa, a follower and adherent of the Pa├▒car─Бtra tradition has undertaken the task of publishing a work of this kind. This indicates that he, like many others who are interested in the publication of works on Pa├▒car─Бtra, is earnest and puts forth his zeal and enthusiasm in undertaking of this kind. He is to be thanked by all scholars of Sanskrit and deserves encouragement for evincing deep interest in these publications.

рдЕрде рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдереЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдордирд╕рд╛рдордзреНрдпреЗрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реМрдХрд░реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╕рдВрдЧреГрд╣реНрдп рдХрдереНрдпрдиреНрддреЗтАФ

  39. Human body is impure made up of matter as it is and so is unfit to make use of it for worshipping God. The worshipper must therefore make the effect merge into its cause. This is a mental process. For instance, odour is to merge in earth which shall get dissolved within taste. Taste shall merge into water and water into colour and so on until, the physical body is felt to have been completely destroyed. The worshipper should then feel receiving the flow of nectar from Viс╣гс╣Зu’s foot on the destroyed body. Then there is produced pure matter which evolves into effects finally bringing a fresh body which shall be made use for worship. This process is called Bh┼лta┼Ыuddhi. ↩︎
